  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_13d4db38-861d-410c-b6ee-e3df510cfa6f'
      });
    }

<div id="review_1187814378" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1187814378" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1187814378?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007326037" href="/book/show/13485199-death-bringer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1187814378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18271030914728481461">OKAY. I CAN'T STAND IT. <b>I LOVE THIS SERIES A CATASTROPHIC AMOUNT.</b> I started thinking, "Yes, I'll be mild fan of this." But pfft, I think I've crossed over to let-me-be-an-obsessive-fan-who-has-a-million-ships-and-cries-a-lot-and-screams-at-the-epic-plot-twists-and-sometimes-howls-because-the-character-development-it-a-thing-of-beauty. The fandom life is nothing if it doesn't consume you, right?<br/><br/>Consider me 100% consumed.<br/><br/>I thought <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8113344.Mortal_Coil__Skulduggery_Pleasant___5_' title='Mortal Coil (Skulduggery Pleasant, #5) by Derek Landy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mortal Coil</a> was mind-blowingly incredible but Death Bringer shoves </span>
  <span id="freeText18271030914728481461" style="display:none">OKAY. I CAN'T STAND IT. <b>I LOVE THIS SERIES A CATASTROPHIC AMOUNT.</b> I started thinking, "Yes, I'll be mild fan of this." But pfft, I think I've crossed over to let-me-be-an-obsessive-fan-who-has-a-million-ships-and-cries-a-lot-and-screams-at-the-epic-plot-twists-and-sometimes-howls-because-the-character-development-it-a-thing-of-beauty. The fandom life is nothing if it doesn't consume you, right?<br /><br />Consider me 100% consumed.<br /><br />I thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8113344.Mortal_Coil__Skulduggery_Pleasant___5_" title="Mortal Coil (Skulduggery Pleasant, #5) by Derek Landy" rel="nofollow noopener">Mortal Coil</a> was mind-blowingly incredible but Death Bringer shoves it out of the spotlight. THIS BOOK WAS SO INTENSE. and the mixture of humour and less-action-y moments was so so perfectly mixed. Although "less action-y moments?" HA. There's only a handful of scenes that start out as "Oh, Valkyrie is actually going to have a restful night and possibly some ice cream, yay! She deserves this!" and then BOOM. Something awful will happen at the end of the chapter -- like Val nearly dying.<br /><br /><b>Although, that is one thing I love a LOT about this series.</b> The main characters are so not above getting hurt. They get HURT SO BAD. Possibly killed and resurrected. It's <i>that</i> kind of book. But you never know if they'll come back okay. HELLO, LET'S NOT TALK ABOUT TANNITH. (Let me cry, but Tannith wasn't even IN this book. Although, I guess, real-Tannith is basically dead and now Remnent-Tannith is on the loose. Boo. But yes, not in the book.) <br /><br /><b>Add in the most INCREDIBLE AND MIND BLOWING PLOT TWIST.</b> It was the kind of twist that I seriously sat there and pouted. And then I stormed off and abandoned this stupid book. THEN I CAME BACK ADN BINGE READ THE LAST 300-PAGES BECAUSE HOLY MACARONI I LOVE THE WRITING AND THE STORY AND THE CHARACTERS. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I cannot <i>believe</i> Skulduggery is Lord Vile!!! Okay. I can. I know he told Val very clearly that his past is awful...but I guess I'd fallen into the "aww, but he'll just have a tragic backstory!" when, in fact, he's like a mass murderer. #awkward But woah. That one just knocked my skull off. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Ohh, let's talk characters, yes?<br />- <b>Skulduggery</b>: Hilarious as ALWAYS of course. Every time he opens his mouth, he's just a little bit more silly and unhinged and so dry you could use his wit as sandpaper. It's wonderful. I LURVE IT. I do feel like he's losing a grip on his sanity though, and this scares me. <br />-<b> Valkyrie</b>: I still struggle to spell her name, but she is without doubt one of my FAVOURITE heroines ever. She's so so awesome! She kicks butt, she has insane powers, she's got inner demons that, um, would like to murder the world. ohhh, AND she makes mistakes. She has some seriously DUMB mistakes that makes me want to slap and shake her. But it does make her more human and relatable...and 16. And she's hilarious. <br />-<b>Fletcher</b>: Well I <i>love</i> Fletcher. I thought he was annoying and dumb at first, but NO. He's incredible. He's matured a LOT since we met him, and...gah. I just really love him. I guess I don't ship him with Val so much <i>anymore</i>, but I really hope he finds friends and things. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I HATED the love-triangle in her. I think it was cliche and stupid...made double worse since Valkyrie KNEW it was so stupid. But Fletcher was so adorable and nice and wonderful and I can't believe she treated him like that. It did make me like Val less, tbh. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />-<b>Celaen:</b> Okay, don't panic: the love-triangle is a teeny tiny part. It's not even a big deal. It gets like 2 chapters in the 600-page book. SO. I do think it's there purely to be a mockery of Twilight. And I kiiiinda hate that. I'm not a Twilight-fan, but I don't like it when books ridicule other authors/books, okay? It's not nice. So I really don't like Cealean and however you spell his name.<br />-<b> Melencholia:</b> Who has a villainous name so dum dum daaaaaa, you can GUESS she sucks in this book!! YAY. I do like her character development, though, because psychopath is always intriguing. (not.)<br />-<b>Alice:</b> AFJDAKLFDJSLFASd VALKYRIE'S BABY SISTER IS NAMED ALICE AND AFJKDLAFDSAFSDJL. IF ANYTHING HAPPENS TO ALICE I WILL PUNCH SOMEONE.<br />-<b> Wreath:</b>...should be slapped.<br />- <b>China:</b>....let's slap her too, yes? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Since she helped murder Skulduggery's family?! ZOMG. WHAT EVEN CHINA. YOU ARE SO MEAN. I TRUSTED YOU. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />-<b>Craven:</b> ...well, we all knew HE wasn't going to end well. <br />-<b> Nye:</b> I'm kinda annoyed that he's being used like the next Kenspeckle...but Nye is a) not a human, b) not sane, c) an it. There is so much wrong with Nye. Plus, you know, that whole thing where he tried to dissect/murder Valkyrie last book. I kinda hate him and I MISS KENSPECKLE SO BAD.<br />-<b>Scapegrace:</b> OMG I LOVE SCAPEGRACE. He's such a loser. He's so dumb and bad and hilarious and he just SUCKS at being evil. I ship him and Thrasher, btw.<br /><br />...aaaand, there are a million characters, so, these are ones I remember, like, um, NOW. I do still get a bit messed up with the characters. I always mess up Wreath and Ghastly WHICH IS DUMB BUT I CAN'T STOP. I'm kind of glad some characters (like Tannith and omg, I've forgotten the American's name..HIM) weren't in, because there was SO SO much to keep a track of. <b>But I still love these characters and I'm so enjoying their journeys and development.</b> I JUST HAVE A LOT OF FEELS. Ohhh, and I HATE how this book ended. That last chapter hurt. me. bad. It makes book 7 be soooo dangerous for Val...on a whole new level. *cries and collapses*<br /><br /><b>Basically, THIS IS AN INSANELY GOOD SERIES.</b> It's like right up there with...with ANY series I read an love, and it absolutely excites me to the core that there's so many books. (I may or may not have just gone and reserved the next THREE from my library. Um, this is the girl who never reads series, okay?! So we know I'm pretty badly addicted.) It's magical and dark and BLOODY and perfect. And hilarious. Did I mention how darn funny it is??!! Okay, okay, lemme prove it.<br /><br /><br /><b>NOTABLE QUOTES OF AWESOME:</b><br /><br /><blockquote>[Skulduggery] "We know how it goes. He says something that annoys you, you get angry, all of a sudden he's lying dead and you're wondering where <i>did</i> the time go."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Dude, I'm sixteen."<br />"I love you."<br />"That doesn't make me any older."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>Skulduggery came back out, shutting the door behind him. "I'm not very good at being pretentious. It's one of my few flaws."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"I don't need to be kept safe all the bloody time."<br />"I see," Skulduggery said. "Well, you make a very good point and I can't argue with your logic. Except I'm not trying to protect you. If I try to open the door and I fail, then I'm going to need someone else to do it once they've killed me. You see?"<br />"Oh," said Valkyrie. "Oh right."<br />"Now if I fail, the odds are that you'll fail too. And if they can kill me, they can most <i>certainly</i> kill you, in an undoubtedly horrible manner. But by then I'll be past caring."<br />"So...you really <i>aren't</i> trying to protect me."<br />"Not even remotely," he said warmly.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"I can't believe you dropped me."<br />"Neither could the people around us. Some crazy woman stormed up and roared at me for five minutes about how I shouldn't be putting my child in danger."<br />"That was me," Valkyrie's mum muttered. </blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"I don't like our chances."<br />"What are our chances?"<br />"We don't have any," Skulduggery admitted.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"I'm not going to just stand by and do nothing," she said through gritted teeth.<br />"You can, as I said, cheer my name, if you want."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>Valkyrie hesitated, then picked up Scapegrace's head. She'd never liked him. The first time she'd met him, he'd tried to throw her off a building. Time and time again, he'd tried to kill her, until his failures actually started to endear him to her. She realised she had begun to view him as a dumb little puppy who would always turn up, sooner or later, to chew on her sock or poo in her shoe. She was going to miss him.</blockquote><br /><br />(That ^^^ is exactly how I feel about Scapegrace. :')<br /><br /><blockquote>"But look on the bright side. Nobody died."<br />Valkyrie frowned. "Lots of people died."<br />"But nobody you <i>like</i>."</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="18271030914728481461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_162789323" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162789323" />
    <a title="Hina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4696625-hina"><img alt="Hina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417298254p2/4696625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162789323?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hina" href="/user/show/4696625-hina">Hina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007326020" href="/book/show/11285163-death-bringer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4696625-hina?shelf=bought">bought</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4696625-hina?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4696625-hina?shelf=just-awesome">just-awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4696625-hina?shelf=awesome-covers">awesome-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4696625-hina?shelf=hina-s-reviews">hina-s-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4696625-hina?shelf=best-characters">best-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4696625-hina?shelf=best-couples">best-couples</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4696625-hina?shelf=characters-i-hate">characters-i-hate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4696625-hina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4696625-hina?shelf=titles-i-love">titles-i-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162789323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3982581175921646303">So I bought this book on September 3rd when I went to Derek Landy's book signing. I had a brilliant time talking to him; he is such a nice person. So when I came home eager to start this book, I was definitely not disappointed. <br/><br/>Melancholia St Clair, an average Necromancer, who has been announced as The Death Bringer, brings shock to the Necromancers, especially Solomon Wreath as he had thought that Valkyrie Cain was the one. The Death Bringer would've been the person to join life and death toget</span>
  <span id="freeText3982581175921646303" style="display:none">So I bought this book on September 3rd when I went to Derek Landy's book signing. I had a brilliant time talking to him; he is such a nice person. So when I came home eager to start this book, I was definitely not disappointed. <br /><br />Melancholia St Clair, an average Necromancer, who has been announced as The Death Bringer, brings shock to the Necromancers, especially Solomon Wreath as he had thought that Valkyrie Cain was the one. The Death Bringer would've been the person to join life and death together by opening up 'The Passage'. But what exactly is this 'Passage'? All the rest of the Sorcerers know is that it will save the world. Or will it? <br /><br />The book is excellent, it maintains it's five star record with a gripping plot and brilliant characters. You can definitely see the growth in the characters, especially Valkyrie's who is now more confident, hormonal, egoistic and far from perfect person. We are told of her brilliance numerous times, but it is balanced out by Fletcher's argument with her which pinpoints all the things that's wrong with her. I thought her character as Darquesse was brilliant, it shows her at her full potential, a very dark and disturbing person indeed. <br /><br />The new characters were slid in very well. I found myself enjoying China Sorrow's manipulation from her old friend, Eliza Scorn. You definitely end up seeing China's subtle side in this book which still includes her smug attitude, but her feelings for Valkyrie develop into something more.<br /><br />I thought that Caelan's character fell, and wasn't the same standard as Derek Landy kept him in the previous books. He was very obsessive over Valkyrie, proposing to her at one point and offering to watch her sleep which reminded me of Edward Cullen. At first I was very disappointed but towards the end I realised that Derek Landy wrote it to take the mickey out of all the Paranormal Romance books that are out there, even having Valkyrie mention Edward and Bella at a point. I was honestly grinning like a fool, but it still doesn't mean that I don't want to throw Caelan off a cliff. <br /><br />There are many twists and turns, many questions get answered, but new ones are also brought up, especially that cliffhanger at the end. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3982581175921646303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10799474561473516792"><blockquote> <b> "Then why put labels on ourselves? That's a job for a psyichiatrist. We punch people, Valkyrie. That's who we are. Embrace your inner lunatic. Fun times guaranteed." </b> </blockquote><br/>It's been a while that I've struggled so much to decide for one quote. This book is full of great quotes that all deserve to head this review and to be read. <br/><blockquote> <b> Glorifying death is not a religion. It's a sickness. </b> </blockquote><br/>I loved this book. It's funny, it's thrilling, it's magical and it has one of the major reveals of the series on its </span>
  <span id="freeText10799474561473516792" style="display:none"><blockquote> <b> "Then why put labels on ourselves? That's a job for a psyichiatrist. We punch people, Valkyrie. That's who we are. Embrace your inner lunatic. Fun times guaranteed." </b> </blockquote><br />It's been a while that I've struggled so much to decide for one quote. This book is full of great quotes that all deserve to head this review and to be read. <br /><blockquote> <b> Glorifying death is not a religion. It's a sickness. </b> </blockquote><br />I loved this book. It's funny, it's thrilling, it's magical and it has one of the major reveals of the series on its pages. You might argue that Valkyrie is arrogant and bitchy in this one (and you would be right...) but I still enjoyed it immensly. Derek Landy has a way with bickering that I haven't seen matched anywhere. I need more right now, I just wanna continue the reread... <br />Plus, the more time I spend rereading this, the more I get on the "I ship Skulduggery and Valkyrie"- train. There is so much hidden in the way they treat each other (which I just might be reading into those line because I'm looking for it) and I think it's glorious. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Although I never expect it to happen and I love them just as much as friends and partners.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3459547650?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan Buckby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan Buckby" href="/user/show/32429909-ryan-buckby">Ryan Buckby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3459547650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17035443786948697003"><b>Embrace your inner lunatic. Fun times guaranteed. </b><br/><br/>This series has and will always step its game up and i have loved every single entry in this series thus far and how far it's come from book one till now. <br/><br/><b> Plot: </b> Book six picks up after the events of book five and we see Valkyrie and Skulduggery trying to stop the necromancers with their plan to cause mass destruction to the world with their new death bringer. I really loved how this series is going and with the direction with how the story is g</span>
  <span id="freeText17035443786948697003" style="display:none"><b>Embrace your inner lunatic. Fun times guaranteed. </b><br /><br />This series has and will always step its game up and i have loved every single entry in this series thus far and how far it's come from book one till now. <br /><br /><b> Plot: </b> Book six picks up after the events of book five and we see Valkyrie and Skulduggery trying to stop the necromancers with their plan to cause mass destruction to the world with their new death bringer. I really loved how this series is going and with the direction with how the story is going i really have no faults with the main plot itself and it's a testament to how strong the writing is. <br /><br />More of Valkyries two worlds are starting to collide and in some way i am really enjoying that fact because its becoming harder for her to keep them seperate. Valkyries two cousins Carol and Crystal now know that she has magical powers and is slowly learning more about the world that she has been brought into after the death of her uncle. I was really surprised to see that the twins father actually knows about the world Valkyrie is apart of and how he doesn't want them apart of it, to me i always thought he didn't know but there was a small part of me that thought he might. <br /><br />Valkyrie starts to become more darker with the way she does things in this one and i think i liked seeing her almost cross that line into no return and it made for some really awesome character development from her and some of her best scenes in the series so far. <br /><br />Finding out that Skulduggery is lord vile was also another shock for me to find out in this one and i'm not really sure if it's been mentioned before in the series but for me finding that out was a real shock. <br /><br /><br /><b>I swear, talking to you is like talking to a really good-looking and mildly stupid brick wall. </b><br /><br />Fletcher and Valkyries relationship turns really rocky in this one and i feel like that it was mostly part to her not really feeling the relationship all that much and towards the end it was more Fletcher putting in the effort than her. However i feel like at her age she is still confused on what she wants and who she likes. I would like this to be explored more as the series goes on. <br /><br /><br />Overall this one was my favourite entry in the series so far and six books in this series just keeps on getting better and better. I can't wait to see were book 7 goes! </span>
  <a data-text-id="17035443786948697003" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer3652677142760814014">4.25-4.5 stars. It's late and I'm tired (as always) so a quick summary here and a proper RTC later.<br/><br/>I really enjoyed this overall, but the unnecessary love triangle/messy cheating subplot was just... annoying and enough for me to kick off half a star. I know she's still a teenager and she's admittedly going through some pretty damn stressful shit, but some of Valkyrie's decisions were frustrating AF. The entire romance subplot was boring and unnecessary imo, so I'm glad it's over now. <s>good riddan</s></span>
  <span id="freeText3652677142760814014" style="display:none">4.25-4.5 stars. It's late and I'm tired (as always) so a quick summary here and a proper RTC later.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this overall, but the unnecessary love triangle/messy cheating subplot was just... annoying and enough for me to kick off half a star. I know she's still a teenager and she's admittedly going through some pretty damn stressful shit, but some of Valkyrie's decisions were frustrating AF. The entire romance subplot was boring and unnecessary imo, so I'm glad it's over now. <s>good riddance to the dead bicth vampire, thank god</s><br /><br />Not 100% sure how I feel about one of the major plot reveals <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Skulduggery being Lord Vile <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and the whole Darquesse situation is starting to feel slightly tedious - I've never been a huge fan of super OP characters when there's nothing to ground them in some way, so that's not surprising. <br /><br />I'm scared for China Sorrows <s>aka my girlfriend</s> after that reveal at the end... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[China being involved in the capture + death of Skulduggery's family <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is probably my favourite twist of the series so I'm super excited to see what ends up happening now that our protagonists know about it.<br /><br />Overall tho, I'm having a blast with this series. I'm all caught up to where I got to in my teens so everything that comes after this is gonna be all new. Onto book seven!</span>

  <span id="freeText1586072216075692180" style="display:none">Oh my God. I just finished this book and it is one of the best in the series, right next to Dark Days.<br /><br />I finished it in 5 days, I could not put it down! Valkyrie has grown up so much. And we discover some SERIOUS stuff about Skulduggery's past! Both of them are ambidextrous mages (so far, at least) and both of them are/were potential Death Bringers. Both of them have a dark alter ego, they even tried to kill each other! But they're best friends, and neither of them can bear to see the other die.<br /><br />Ships have sunk: Valkyrie/Fletcher, Valkyrie/Caelan, Skulduggery/China. All of this is paving the path for Valkyrie/Skulduggery! <br /><br />And this is the first book without Tanith in it, except for mention by name. I feel so sorry for poor Ghastly, he was SO CLOSE to being with her! There's not much of him in this book, sadly, but he DID say some of the most important lines, to Fletcher.<br /><br />The Requim Ball was definitely for all those fans who have written fanfiction about a Sanctuary Ball! Valkyrie was amazing, and boy, Skulduggery can DANCE! With China... e<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www">www</a>....<br /><br />Lots of shocking revelations and events happen in this book. The final trilogy will be something that is very different from the first two.</span>

<div id="review_336852115" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/336852115" />
    <a title="Robert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1433865-robert"><img alt="Robert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1254324661p2/1433865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/336852115?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert" href="/user/show/1433865-robert">Robert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007326037" href="/book/show/13485199-death-bringer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1433865-robert?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer336852115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15255994482434937995">Skulduggery 6 represents a return to form for Landy, mainly because he shakes things up quite a bit; Tanith and Sanguine are no-shows, other characters are bogged down in bureaucracy and there are quite a number of surprising revelations.<br/><br/>At the end of the previous volume I thought I had worked out quite a bit of what was going to happen next; none of it played out the way I expected, though some of it still might...because the Reflection subplot <i>still</i> hasn't paid off...which is getting a little </span>
  <span id="freeText15255994482434937995" style="display:none">Skulduggery 6 represents a return to form for Landy, mainly because he shakes things up quite a bit; Tanith and Sanguine are no-shows, other characters are bogged down in bureaucracy and there are quite a number of surprising revelations.<br /><br />At the end of the previous volume I thought I had worked out quite a bit of what was going to happen next; none of it played out the way I expected, though some of it still might...because the Reflection subplot <i>still</i> hasn't paid off...which is getting a little irritating...I also thought vol. 6 was going to wrap things up; no more Skeleton Detective stories. How wrong can I be? There's already a World Book Day novelette following on from this book...<br /><br />With Kenspeckle also out of the picture, Landy needed to find another approach to the, "Skulduggery is a bad influence on Valkyrie," voice. This he manages by working it into the story via the protagonists' actions and hidden aspects. This works much better than another lecture by the good doctor would have. In fact Cain behaves pretty unpleasantly in various respects during the course of the book and only retains sympathy because of the previous five books. It's brave on the part of Landy and I applaud it. It's a shame, however, that one of the ways Cain behaves badly is during the Anti-Twilight plot-line. I could have lived without it; it's not even remotely subtle and I certainly don't need a warning about the unwisdom of a teen having a "romance" with a stalker-over-protector-controlling older man... Maybe the target audience (i.e. actual teenagers) <i>do</i> need such a warning but I'd like to think they don't, even if they are rabid Twilight fans. I could tell life and novels apart when I was a teen.<br /><br />But is this series <i>ever</i> going to end? At least could Landy write something else between Skeleton Detective tomes? I want to believe he has more than one idea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15255994482434937995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_205908304" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205908304" />
    <a title="Conor McHugh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3998138-conor-mchugh"><img alt="Conor McHugh" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205908304?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Conor McHugh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Conor McHugh" href="/user/show/3998138-conor-mchugh">Conor McHugh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007326020" href="/book/show/11285163-death-bringer">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205908304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12416899088168336773">I borrowed the first Skulduggery book a few years back, when i was on my fishing trip to Ireland. (My family have this house in Donegal, which has been passed down the family). When i started reading it of course, i realised that it was actually SET in Ireland, how friggin' awesome.<br/><br/>...So there i was in Ireland, reading Skulduggery Pleasant, as you do. And i thought it was pretty snazzy.<br/><br/>Then i read "playing with fire". Meh.<br/>"Faceless ones" Kinda good.<br/>"Dark Days" amazing.<br/>"Mortal Coil" Wow.<br/><br/>And then </span>
  <span id="freeText12416899088168336773" style="display:none">I borrowed the first Skulduggery book a few years back, when i was on my fishing trip to Ireland. (My family have this house in Donegal, which has been passed down the family). When i started reading it of course, i realised that it was actually SET in Ireland, how friggin' awesome.<br /><br />...So there i was in Ireland, reading Skulduggery Pleasant, as you do. And i thought it was pretty snazzy.<br /><br />Then i read "playing with fire". Meh.<br />"Faceless ones" Kinda good.<br />"Dark Days" amazing.<br />"Mortal Coil" Wow.<br /><br />And then i saw Death Bringer. I'd almost forgot about Skulduggery, but i nabbed the book off the shelf at TESCO'S ASAP. And my god, this series has FINALLY, officially, completely won me over. <br /><br />Everything about it, the characters, dialogue, story, is brilliant, beyond comparison. I haven't been able to relate to the previous books as well, i think this is because it took this book for me to finally tune into the right wave length. Next time i read the previous books, ill probably love them more.<br /><br />This book has so many awesome quotes that i'll never forget.<br /><br />The romance is hilarious. Constantly laughing in Bella and Edwards face. Taking the Mick out of Paranormal romances, iv'e never smiled so much whilst reading. Here's a couple of epic quotes:<br /><br />Valkyrie to Caelan - "were not Buffy and Angel, or Romeo and Juliet, or those two from west side story. Were not even Edward and Bella, OK? You're far too freaky for me."<br /><br />Fletcher to Caelan - "Just listening to you makes me want to top myself, you self-pitying paranormal romance reject"<br /><br /><br />AAAH GAAD EPICNESS.<br /><br />If i am ever in a fight with someone, right before i punch them, i will make sure i say "the Sparrow flies south for winter"<br />Read the book, then you will understand.<br /><br />I mean it though. Read it.<br />Now.<br />Read the others before though, or you won't have a clue what you're reading.<br /><br />This is almost the first series to come along that i can say has NEARLY replaced that little gaping hole that the end of the Harry Potter books left. Bring on more Derek Landy, you genious.<br />5 stars!<br /><br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007326051" href="/book/show/12351174-death-bringer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer255658516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16256927134538297615">A decent edition to the series, even darker and more dangers than before, but not one of my faves. Was disappointed that not much about the situation with Tanith was really dealt with.<br/><br/>While I enjoyed the book well enough overall, there were a few issues. For one, the pacing was off and definitely dragged in places - and some of the fight scenes, especially the last one... ye gods. The snark and humor is still good when Valkyrie and Skulduggery are bantering, but seemed sadly lacking any other ti</span>
  <span id="freeText16256927134538297615" style="display:none">A decent edition to the series, even darker and more dangers than before, but not one of my faves. Was disappointed that not much about the situation with Tanith was really dealt with.<br /><br />While I enjoyed the book well enough overall, there were a few issues. For one, the pacing was off and definitely dragged in places - and some of the fight scenes, especially the last one... ye gods. The snark and humor is still good when Valkyrie and Skulduggery are bantering, but seemed sadly lacking any other time.<br /><br />But my main issue was that Valkyrie isn't really very relatable. While I enjoy some of the snark and whatnot, she's just not very likable a lot of the term. You need to have a good side and qualities to counter the dark ones, and in this one she's mostly dark.<br /><br />And I'm sort of tired of the whole insta-heal stuff. It just doesn't give the events a whole lot of suspense and immediacy.<br /><br />I was torn about the one reveal, namely <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that Skulduggery was/is Lord Vile. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> While it puts him in a unique position to understand the Darquesse situation, it also had a bit of a "really?" vibe to it. Like how much can possibly be wrapped up in these two?<br /><br />Still fully plan on continuing with the series, and I'm nowhere near wanting to give up on it, but I'm also still hoping it gets better. It seems like it's kinda circling the airport at this point, so to speak.</span>

<div id="review_2813991765" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2813991765" />
    <a title="Highness Atharva" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47064311-highness-atharva"><img alt="Highness Atharva" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588967638p2/47064311.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2813991765?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Highness Atharva" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Highness Atharva" href="/user/show/47064311-highness-atharva">Highness Atharva</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2813991765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5470505146071439731">Skulduggery Pleasant Book 6<br/>*Death Bringer* by Derek Landy<br/>Just when you think you have seen it all, Mr Landy swoops in and builds a much more enormous and intricate magical world with magnanimous details, lore and secondary characters which of course, are the elements on which the series thrives. As we all know the story has/had an insane narration pace, here it feels inconsistent mostly because of Valkyrie's unstable teenage romannce which takes up around 10% of the entirety of the book and thor</span>
  <span id="freeText5470505146071439731" style="display:none">Skulduggery Pleasant Book 6<br />*Death Bringer* by Derek Landy<br />Just when you think you have seen it all, Mr Landy swoops in and builds a much more enormous and intricate magical world with magnanimous details, lore and secondary characters which of course, are the elements on which the series thrives. As we all know the story has/had an insane narration pace, here it feels inconsistent mostly because of Valkyrie's unstable teenage romannce which takes up around 10% of the entirety of the book and thoroughly disappointing, not the bit with Fletcher but with Caelan and I'm really glad the author decided to give him a fancy death at the end of the book. There are a lot of elements that dictate the proceeding of the story along with multitude of character interactions we have never seen before like Kenny, the reporter, the street mugger, Dragonclaw, the necromancers, the Warlock (a race which we believed was extinct), the Twin Sisters of Havoc, Clarabelle, Nye, The League of Dead Men, Eliza Scorn, Melancholia (fancy name, character sucks), Craven, Wreath, The Sensitives, Lord Vile, Scapegrace and the Zombie Horde, Fletcher and the newly appointed Sanctuary leaders all play a noticeable if not major every single time role in the book. The way the plot moves is almost flawless with superb transitions and the author bides his time with character secrets and reveals them at a time creating the most impact. I almost do not have any complaints about the book as Mr Landy uplifts the readers to new heights with everything fresh with new depth and detail, a bit complicated but highly entertaining. I loved the reveal of Lord Vile's character being a subconscious of Skulduggery and the whole history lesson with regard to that. The League of the Dead Men introduced at the requiem Ball seems very fancy and may recur in further installments. Nye and Clarabelle working together? It can't get more weird! No Tanith/Billy-Ray Sanguine? A bit disappointing! Kenny, the reporter's takes on the Magical Community? Something's Fish! Valkyrie-Fletcher-Caelan love triangle? Sorry, I don't dig that. Let me talk about the necromancers in the book as the philosophical idea of 'Death Bringer' mostly relates to these outcast members of the society looking for the perfect person who can instantaneously kill 3B people for their salvation and permenance upon the Earth. The idea seemed so enormous and fancy at first but I didn't imagine Solomon Wreath would aid them but the part played out very well. Melancholia's visual appeal was superb but every single word coming out of her mouth, every line of dialogue seemed cheesy, corny and trivial like she did not really have an idealistic motive but a soiled adult with superpowers capable of destroying the entire magical community. Mostly, this had an intrisinic villainous roots with Eliza Scorn and Dragonclaw also kicking the protagonists a few times. Mostly, Lord Vile just swept his hands and the rest would be done by the shadows, that part totally engrossed me. A lot has been happening with Valkyrie's family, Alice, The Toxic Twins an the reveal that Fergus knows a bit of magic totally shocked me, it was so unexpected. The final battle between Lord Vile and Darquesse rose to epic heights than I'd expect. I'm very much excited for the future of the series, the author has thrown in some key plot points which may aid the story in the future installments. I thoroughly enjoyed this. Nice Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5470505146071439731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_345575496" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/345575496" />
    <a title="Jenvile" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10112966-jenvile"><img alt="Jenvile" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603890015p2/10112966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/345575496?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenvile" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenvile" href="/user/show/10112966-jenvile">Jenvile</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007466795" href="/book/show/13612716-death-bringer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10112966-jenvile?shelf=scifi-fantasy">scifi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10112966-jenvile?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer345575496&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer345575496" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3499410180178683231">It’s my 10 Year Anniversary with Skulduggery Pleasant, the book series that changed my life. In this re-read, I’ll be doing something special. I’ll be rounding up my top 10 favourite moments from each book, and quoting the scenes that I love the most. Obviously this will come with spoilers, SO DON’T READ THIS IF YOU HAVEN’T READ THE SERIES.<br/><br/>Death Bringer is always in the fight to climb higher and higher in my top favourites within the series, and without a doubt, it definitely earns its place wit</span>
  <span id="freeText3499410180178683231" style="display:none">It’s my 10 Year Anniversary with Skulduggery Pleasant, the book series that changed my life. In this re-read, I’ll be doing something special. I’ll be rounding up my top 10 favourite moments from each book, and quoting the scenes that I love the most. Obviously this will come with spoilers, SO DON’T READ THIS IF YOU HAVEN’T READ THE SERIES.<br /><br />Death Bringer is always in the fight to climb higher and higher in my top favourites within the series, and without a doubt, it definitely earns its place within the top 5. I think this quote in the beginning is the best aphorism that describes this book:<br /><br /><i>”Good and evil are so close together as to be chained together in the soul.” (Dr Jekyll and Mr Hyde)</i><br /><br />So many moments. So many. God it’s like one bombshell after another, and after one bombshell there’s just more bombshells. It’ll be so hard to narrow down my favourites but here they are, which I’m giving reluctantly because I really don’t know if these are my top moments because there’s so many more that I want to add.<br /><br />10. The Jitter Girls. Absolutely frightening little things aren’t they?<br /><br /><i>”What is it?” she whispered.<br />“It’s a box,” he whispered back.<br />“What kind of box?”<br />“A wooden one.”<br />She gave him a look. “OK, I’ll try this. Why are we hiding from a box?”<br />“We’re not. We’re hiding from what’s inside the box.”<br />“What’s in the box?”<br />“Is it a head?” Fletcher asked.<br />“It’s the Jitter Girls.”</i><br /><br />9. When Darquesse comes out during their Jitter Girls fight - DAMNNN I am obsessed with this little encounter.<br /><br /><i> “Hello,” he said. “I’ve been waiting for you.”<br />Darquesse smiled, walking towards him.<br />“You’re very impressive,” he continued. “That’s a kind of magic I don’t think I’ve ever seen, and I’ve seen every kind of magic. You are quite the curiosity, aren’t you?” </i><br /><br />8. Melancholia showing up at Val’s house and... slashing... her... to... ribbons. <br /><br /><i> “I could destroy you and no one would be able to do anything about it. I would tear you from your family. Your friends would be powerless to stop me. The Skeleton Detective? I’d make him watch.”<br />Valkyrie said nothing.</i><br /><br />And then Skulduggery’s reaction to it after through Ghastly’s eyes. *chefs kiss*<br /><br /><i>”And how are you?” Ghastly said.<br />“Meaning?”<br />“She was almost killed.”<br />“I am aware. You’re waiting to see if I’ll get angry.”<br />“I already know you’re angry. You’re sitting very still and you’re talking very quietly. You’re getting ready to kill someone.”<br />“I just need a name.”</i><br /><br />7. Fletcher and Caelan at the end of the book. I really enjoyed Fletcher’s character here, he’s just hilarious.<br /><br /><i>Caelan took a breath, like he was in pain, and straightened up. His voice was low, guttural. “I was hoping I’d get the chance to kill you.”<br />“You won’t be killing anyone, you sad little emo git.”<br />“You’ve stood in the way of our love for long enough.”<br />“Just listening to you makes me want to top myself, you self-pitying Paranormal Romance reject.”<br />Caelan glared. “Stop insulting me.”<br />“Why? If you cry, will your mascara run?”</i><br /><br />6. What’s the best code for when you’re about to punch someone?<br /><br /><i>”Very well. How about the sparrow flies south for winter?”<br />“Seriously?”<br />“What’s wrong with it? It’s a classic.”</i><br /><br />5. The Requiem Ball!!!!<br /><br /><i> “You’re late,” he said.<br />“I’m beautiful.”<br />“You’re always beautiful.”<br />“I’m always late, too.”</i><br /><br />4. Darquesse and Lord Vile’s EPIC. FIGHT.<br /><br /><i>”Darquesse stood up, and looked at Lord Vile. “Be honest,” she said. “You’ve been looking forward to this, haven’t you?”</i><br /><br />3. The. Big. Reveal. <br /><br /><i>“He abandoned his old life. He wore armour to disguise his old form. He took a new name to kill his old self.”<br />“No,” Valkyrie said. “No, don’t.”<br />“Skulduggery Pleasant walked off the battlefield, and Lord Vile walked into my Temple.”</i><br /><br />2. Probably my favourite scene of all time in Death Bringer - when Skulduggery came through and tried to call out to Valkyrie and then the banter that we all know and love after this scene... I’m getting emotional just thinking about this.<br /><br /><i>“Valkyrie,” Lord Vile said. His voice was a whisper.<br />Darquesse smiled. “I’m Valkyrie. Whatever you’ve got to say to her, you can say to me. What was it Skulduggery said earlier? I’m her bad mood.”<br />That whisper again. “Let her out.”</i><br /><br />1. China’s. Secret. <br /><br /><i>”I won’t blame you,” she said, her voice tight with pain, “if you walk away.”<br />“Good,” Valkyrie said, and she did just that.</i><br /><br />Honourable mention:<br /><br />Melancholia and Valkyrie’s unlikely friendship by the end of the book: <br /><br /><i>”What are you trying to do?”<br />“I’m trying to take his soul.”<br />Valkyrie punched her, right across the jaw. “I’m not going to let you kill him, you nutcase. You think I’d ever choose you over him?”</i><br /><br />This one was quite a heavy book! There are so many big reveals and it felt like such a huge payoff after all the other books previous to it. Of course, this one caps off the Death Bringer/necromancer trilogy, and while that’s been fun - the really nifty gritty is the Darquesse trilogy....<br /><br />———<br /><br />Excerpts from: Skulduggery Pleasant: Death Bringer by Derek Landy. Copyright HarperCollins Publishing, review under fair use.</span>

<div id="review_258308367" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258308367" />
    <a title="Darren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3530438-darren"><img alt="Darren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326022184p2/3530438.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258308367?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darren" href="/user/show/3530438-darren">Darren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007326020" href="/book/show/11285163-death-bringer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3530438-darren?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3530438-darren?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3530438-darren?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3530438-darren?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258308367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11145958333482470732">I have spent some time agonising over how to write this review without giving away any spoilers, and the only thing I can think of is to make it shorter than most of my reviews. There is just so much happening in this book that it is nigh impossible to say much at all about the story without giving something away that may spoil the book for the few die-hard fans out there who have not yet read it. I will do my utmost however, although if you have not yet read Mortal Coil, the fifth book in the s</span>
  <span id="freeText11145958333482470732" style="display:none">I have spent some time agonising over how to write this review without giving away any spoilers, and the only thing I can think of is to make it shorter than most of my reviews. There is just so much happening in this book that it is nigh impossible to say much at all about the story without giving something away that may spoil the book for the few die-hard fans out there who have not yet read it. I will do my utmost however, although if you have not yet read Mortal Coil, the fifth book in the series, then I suggest you navigate away from this page now.<br /><br />Mortal Coil was an incredibly dark book, and as I mentioned in my review last year, one of my favourite in the series so far. There were so many great revelations, and the climactic scenes had me gasping for breath, especially regarding the fate of one of my favourite characters, Tanith Low. However, Death Bringer may have just usurped Mortal Coil and could now be my favourite book in the series, although the complete absence of Tanith from the story was a slight disappointment. So what makes it so good? I think the best way of doing this without giving away spoilers is in list form, so in no particular order:<br /><br />The dialogue. It's brilliant, and there seems to be so much more of it in this book. In fact, I think the increased dialogue between Sulduggery and Valkyrie is possibly the main contributing factor to the book's length. Derek Landy has created so many great characters, but what makes them stand out so much is the banter between them, and especially between his two main protagonists. It is consistently funny, occasionally poignant, and shows the deep bond that has grown between these two over the course of their adventures together.<br /><br />The action. There are some amazing action scenes in this book, and they are some of the best we have seen from the author. There was one scene where I suddenly started choking as I had not realised that I had been holding my breath and my lungs need to breath suddenly caught up with my brain's fixation on the story I was reading.<br /><br />More character development. Some of Landy's characters have remained pretty much on the sidelines of the main plot so far in the series, and although ever present we still do not know a great deal about them. One such characters is China Sorrows, and in Death Bringer we find out a great deal more about her history, and it is far from being good.<br /><br />More revelations. I don't think I am particularly stupid so I hope I wasn't the only one who did not see one particular revelation about Skulduggery coming. In fact, I was so surprised that I think my brain went into shut down, and I spent a good five minutes just staring at the page in shock.<br /><br />I've saved the best until last..... Valkyrie and Skulduggery. There will be moments in this book when you may actually find yourself disliking these two, and Val in particular. It is easy to forget that she is just a teenager, and yet she has achieved so much and seen so many horrors at such a young age. What kind of effect would that have on a teenager? In Death Bringer we really start to find out. We see her ego, her selfishness, her betrayal of trust, her moodiness - at times she becomes a thoroughly unlikeable young lady, and the story is all the better for it.<br /> <br />Another great addition to the Skulduggery series, and it continues to be one of my favourite series around at the moment. It is just a pity that we will probably have to wait another year for Book Seven in the series. However, SP fans, make sure you hit the book stores in March 2012 as Derek Landy is contributing a Skulduggery Pleasant novelette for World Book Day, called The End of the World. This book will be set after the events of Death Bringer, but whether Tanith will feature I do not know. Whatever the outcome, I have a feeling that she will feature quite heavily in Skulduggery Pleasant Book Seven, and I am sure it won't be good for Valkyrie or Skulduggery.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11145958333482470732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nFxFqGCVMBZY/t4E3/X9UxaUIa96w7MqC21UO0nyY8UolHR07OvkINsG9ZObWcC6zcw6LYAp/uJQpK9zbxxMPw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yVPJMQ1D38IS6VHYhNudsPkQP6EBlO7nMFKE9Vi5trh9m/jtgT0L9JERek/Ad6BZIkgkI/t+oy9rm3+9fleZQg==')})
  }
//]]>

The Hollow Boy Lockwood &amp; Co. might be the smallest (some might say shambollic) Psychic Detection Agency in London. But its three agents - Lockwood, Lucy and George - are exceptional Talents. The Empty Grave After their recent adventures, the Lockwood &amp; Co team deserve a well-earned break . . . so naturally they decide to risk their lives breaking into a heavily-guarded crypt. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6746115-on-myself-and-other-less-important-subjects"><img alt="On Myself, and Other, Less Important Subjects" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1348329263l/6746115._SX98_.jpg" />

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_6746115'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6746115-on-myself-and-other-less-important-subjects?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">On Myself, and Other, Less Important Subjects<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/3035509.Caspar_Hare?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Caspar Hare<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.94 avg rating &mdash; 16 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2009\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer5505139686373729284\">Caspar Hare makes an original and compelling case for egocentric presentism, a view about the nature of first-person experience, about what happens when we see things from our own particular point of view. A natural thought about our first-person exp<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText5505139686373729284\" style=\"display:none\">Caspar Hare makes an original and compelling case for egocentric presentism, a view about the nature of first-person experience, about what happens when we see things from our own particular point of view. A natural thought about our first-person experience is that all and only the things of which I am aware are present to me. Hare, however, goes one step further and claims, counterintuitively, that the thought should instead be that all and only the things of which I am aware are present. There is, in other words, something unique about me and the things of which I am aware.\n\n\n\nOn Myself and Other, Less Important Subjects represents a new take on an old view, known as solipsism, which maintains that people\'s experiences give them grounds for believing that they have a special, distinguished place in the world--for example, believing that only they exist or that other people do not have conscious minds like their own. Few contemporary thinkers have taken solipsism seriously. But Hare maintains that the version of solipsism he argues for is in indeed defensible, and that it is uniquely capable of resolving some seemingly intractable philosophical problems--both in metaphysics and ethics--concerning personal identity over time, as well as the tension between self-interest and the greater good.\n\n This formidable and tightly argued defense of a seemingly absurd view is certain to provoke debate.\n\n-- &quot;Choice&quot;<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"5505139686373729284\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13628517078570274366">Derek Landy is an Irish writer and screenwriter. In addition to the bestselling children's/YA series of <i>Skulduggery Pleasant</i> books, a supernatural mystery series starring Skulduggery Pleasant, a skeleton detective, and Valkyrie Cain, a young female magician, he has written two screenplays that have been made into films: the IFTA award winning "Dead Bodies" and the IFTA nominated "Boy Eats Girl". L</span>
  <span id="freeText13628517078570274366" style="display:none">Derek Landy is an Irish writer and screenwriter. In addition to the bestselling children's/YA series of <i>Skulduggery Pleasant</i> books, a supernatural mystery series starring Skulduggery Pleasant, a skeleton detective, and Valkyrie Cain, a young female magician, he has written two screenplays that have been made into films: the IFTA award winning "Dead Bodies" and the IFTA nominated "Boy Eats Girl". Landy himself was nominated for an IFTA for Best Script. <br /><br />He doesn’t like to brag about all the awards he’s won, such as the Irish Book of the Decade, or the Red House in the UK, or all the other awards that he humbly displays on his mantelpiece. He is also far too modest to mention things like the first book being a Publisher’s Weekly Best Book of the Year, but would like to extend an invitation to Oprah to pop around one day for tea, in thanks for selecting his book for the Oprah’s Book Club Kids Reading List. <br /><br />Derek plays too many video games, reads too many comics, and watches too many movies. He lives in Ireland with too many cats. Occasionally he talks to real people, but only when he absolutely has to.</span>
